# Microsoft Teams Essential Training

> Discover the core features of Microsoft Teams and find out how you can bring together colleagues, create conversations and content, and collaborate more effectively and efficiently. Author Nick Brazzi takes you through the essentials of using Teams, starting with basic setup, creating new teams, and joining existing teams. Nick covers organizing teams and members, shows you how to conduct conversa

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395) | 3h 46m | 8K learners

#### Communicate effectively with Microsoft Teams
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=0)** - Communication is one of the biggest keys to success in the workplace.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=4)** Microsoft Teams offers several tools to make that communication easier.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=8)** I'm Nick Brazzi, and I've put together a training course that introduces the most important features in Teams, including group conversation threads and established team channels.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=18)** Private chats let you send messages to specific people which are not visible to others.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=24)** You can also do private audio and video calls, and then there are meetings, which can be scheduled ahead of time, giving you plenty of options for face-to-face communication with remote team members.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/communicate-effectively-with-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=35)** This course is mainly targeted to users of Teams for business, Enterprise and Education, but even if you are using the free version or using Teams as a guest, there's still great information for you here.

#### Understand the different versions of Teams
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980)

> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=1)** - There are different versions of Microsoft Teams, which have different sets of features, and there are optional add-ons available that can add even more features.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=10)** So there may be some features that you'll see in this course that you do not have in your version of Teams.
>

>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=26)** This course mainly focuses on the version of Microsoft Teams for enterprise and large businesses.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=32)** This is the version of Teams that comes with a Microsoft 365 subscription, that is usually purchased for a company, organization, or school by that organization's IT department.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=43)** This is sometimes referred to as the full version of Teams.
>

>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=59)** A Microsoft Teams Essentials, Business Basic, or Business Standard subscription is usually purchased by a business owner who can then invite their coworkers to join and use Teams with them.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=70)** If you use one of these subscriptions, then most of the features that you'll see in this course will work for you, but there are some features that you will not have.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=78)** Okay, let's back up again to that main page.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=81)** And Microsoft Teams for Education is a variation of Teams that focuses on organizing schools or classrooms, instead of businesses and work groups.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=91)** It's got great features for making classroom assignments.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=94)** While this course mostly shows the Enterprise version of Teams, most features will work the same in the Education version.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=101)** And there are some videos in this course that focus on some of the differences and specific features in the Education version.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=107)** Now, the Home version of Teams is the most different from the others.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=111)** Teams for Home users looks completely different and has far fewer features, because it's not designed to be used in a workplace.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=119)** Some of the content in this course about private chats, video calls, and meetings will help Home users, but for the most part, this course is not for Home users.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=130)** So those are the different versions of Teams.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=133)** However, there are two popular add-ons that are available, which add extra features to Teams for enterprise or education.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=140)** Both of these add-ons require a separate purchase, so your Microsoft administrator would need to buy a license for these add-ons before you can use those features.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=149)** And if you want to use some of the exciting artificial intelligence features in Teams, those generally come with these add-ons.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=158)** Microsoft 365 Copilot is an add-on for a Microsoft 365 subscription in an organization.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=165)** This adds an AI assistant to several Microsoft 365 applications, including Word, Outlook, PowerPoint, Excel, and Microsoft Teams.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=176)** If you have the Copilot add-on and you work in Teams, you can use an AI assistant that can summarize or answer questions about your chat conversations or meetings.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=186)** Teams Premium is a completely different add-on which is used only in Teams.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=191)** It does not offer new features for other Microsoft applications.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=194)** Teams Premium also requires the purchase of a separate license.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=198)** It is available for enterprise or education subscriptions, and it adds several high-level security features, customization options, and it includes an AI-powered meeting summary tool.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=209)** Later in this course, we will see an introduction to the main Copilot features in Teams and some features in Teams Premium.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=217)** Finally, it is important to understand that the Enterprise and Education versions of Teams are purchased by a Microsoft administrator at your company or school.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=227)** This person is responsible for managing Teams and deciding which features are enabled for all of the users in your organization.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=235)** So if there's a feature that you need to be enabled or disabled, or you need one of these add-ons, you should communicate with the Microsoft 365 administrator at your company or school, and that's usually somebody in your IT department.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=250)** And keep in mind that Microsoft updates Teams and those add-ons very often.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=256)** As you go through this course, you may see some features that look a little different.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/understand-the-different-versions-of-teams?u=76281980&t=260)** So be prepared for changes and be aware of some features that are only available in specific versions of Microsoft Teams.

#### Use Teams on the web or the desktop application
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] When you use Teams, you can sign in directly on the Teams website or you can use a separate application that you install on your computer.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=8)** We'll start by using Teams in a web browser.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=10)** Any user, regardless of your subscription type, can go to Teams.[microsoft.com](https://microsoft.com).
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=16)** This will work in most web browsers, including Chrome, Microsoft Edge, and Safari.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=21)** You will need to sign in with your account.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=24)** If you have a Microsoft 365 email address and password set up and managed by your company or school, that's what you should use to sign in, or if you're using a Team's essential subscription, you may have set up the account when you bought the subscription, or maybe a team leader sent you an invitation.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=41)** You'll need to follow the prompts in that invitation email to set up the account that you'll use to sign into Teams.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=47)** So you should have your account ready and use it to sign in here, and it will sign you into the appropriate version of Teams for your subscription.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=59)** Now, let's see another way to sign in on the web.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=61)** If you are a Microsoft 365 subscriber, you can go to the Microsoft 365 website.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-on-the-web-or-the-desktop-application?u=76281980&t=67)** That is [office.com](https://office.com), and if you sign in this way, you have access to lots of different Microsoft tools.
>

#### Use Teams as a guest: Client and contractor access

> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=6)** The Business, Enterprise, and Education versions of Teams are all built around organizations.

>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=181)** Let's see some of those limitations.

>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=193)** So when guests are invited to a meeting, they will receive an email with a link to join that meeting.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=199)** Guests can participate in team conversations but cannot create their own new teams.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=204)** Also, any features that require a connection to the Microsoft 365 ecosystem will not work.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=210)** This includes things like SharePoint integration.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=212)** But the benefit is that guest users can work with members of an established organization without being a full member of that organization.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=220)** Guests can participate in conversation channels, file sharing in those channels, private chats, video calls and meetings with the normal members of the organization.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=230)** You can see how this could be vital for independent contractors or probationary employees who need to be engaged in team projects but are not officially employees of the company.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-teams-as-a-guest-client-and-contractor-access?u=76281980&t=240)** Since there are many features that work the same for guest users, much of this course will be useful even for guests.

> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=72)** Why?
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=73)** Well, it's because of a new feature that allows you to combine the Chat and the Teams section into one.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=79)** Near the top right, next to My Account icon, I'll click the button with three dots to open this menu, then go to Settings.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=87)** And in Settings, we'll go to the category for Chats and Channels.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=91)** And here, you can choose to keep your Chat section and your Teams section separate or combined.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=97)** I have this set to Separate, so I see both buttons on the sidebar.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=100)** But if I choose Combined, now, the Teams button is gone from the sidebar.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=106)** And if I click the Chat button, here in the Chat section, I can see my list of recent chat conversations and my teams and channels all in one place.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=115)** So this combines your private chats and public team conversations into one section in the application interface.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=122)** And this is 100% your choice.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=125)** You can decide whether you want the Chat and Teams combined or separate.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=130)** But as you watch me work in this course, I will keep them separated, not because I prefer that or recommend that setup, it's because I find it easier to explain and easier to understand how everything works if we keep them separated.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=143)** So I'll go back into Settings, back to that Chats and Channels section, and I'll switch this to the Separate mode.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=153)** When you do this, it may ask for some feedback explaining why you want to switch back to the Separate mode.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=158)** For now, I'll just click Cancel, and we can see that the Separate mode is set.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=163)** And now, I have separate buttons in the sidebar for Chat and Teams.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=168)** But I should mention that there is another reason why you might not see one of the buttons here in the sidebar, It is possible to unpin these buttons.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=177)** You can right-click on a button and you see the unpin option.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=180)** So if I unpin the Calendar button, that button is gone from the sidebar.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=185)** If that's the case, and if you want it back, you can click the button with three dots in the sidebar and you'll find the missing button there.

> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=197)** And you can also drag these buttons up or down to change the order.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=201)** And what we see here is more or less the default layout.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/keep-teams-and-chats-combined-or-separated?u=76281980&t=205)** If you're new to Teams, I recommend you start with this layout.
>

### 3. Group Conversations using Teams and Channels

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Organize conversations with channels
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/organize-conversations-with-channels-25634941?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/organize-conversations-with-channels-25634941?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] All of the conversations you have in your Teams will be organized into channels.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/organize-conversations-with-channels-25634941?u=76281980&t=5)** We use channels to organize different conversation topics, and channels are listed under each team name.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/organize-conversations-with-channels-25634941?u=76281980&t=11)** You can click the triangle next to a team name to hide or to show the channels contained in it.
>

> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/create-private-or-shared-channels?u=76281980&t=243)** And if you are a member of a team and you see a channel with this icon, it means that it is a shared channel.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/create-private-or-shared-channels?u=76281980&t=249)** So there might be people who are not members of the larger team, contributing to the discussion here.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/create-private-or-shared-channels?u=76281980&t=254)** And if you are added to a shared channel without being added as a member to the team that contains it, then you will see that team listed with only that shared channel and you will not see any of the other channels in the team.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/create-private-or-shared-channels?u=76281980&t=267)** So for the most part, if you are a member of a team, you may not need to worry about whether a channel is a standard channel, private channel, or shared channel.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/create-private-or-shared-channels?u=76281980&t=275)** You can just choose a channel, and join the conversation.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/create-private-or-shared-channels?u=76281980&t=279)** But if you are a team owner, or if you need to create new channels in a team, it's good to know that there are some more versatile types of channels.

> [!info]- Semantic Content

> **CLI Commands:** make (4), find (2)
> **UI Navigation:** open the (3)
> **Analogies:** just like (2)

#### Target messages with @mentions
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] When you post a message, you can use @ mentions, which can specifically refer to a member of your team, and targets that message at them to draw their attention.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=9)** I'm working in my web design team, in the channel called Site Redesign, and I'm going to reply to an existing conversation thread.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=16)** I'll start typing in my message.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=23)** Then I want to refer to a specific person, so I'll use an @ mention.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=27)** To do that, you can start by typing the @ symbol and do not type a space.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=31)** Immediately after the @ symbol, start typing in that person's name and it will search through the members of this team.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=38)** I found the person I was looking for, so I can click on him, and this is what an @ mention looks like, I can see that person's name in a different color, and you can actually feel free to delete the last name and just keep the first name, so you can keep things a little more informal, and then finish typing the rest of your message.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=59)** And then I can hit the return key or click the send button to send that message.

>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=98)** I can also see a number one on the teams button in the sidebar on the left and on the activity button.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=104)** I'll go to the activity section where you can see recent notifications and I can see the message that was posted and the response, which contains an @ mention targeted at me, or I could just go to that team.

>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=172)** So I could type the @ symbol, and then follow that with Brand Material to make an @ mention targeted at that Brand Material channel.

> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=180)** Now, this is not used as often, but what this will do is send a notification alert to every member of that team to let them know that that team or that channel was mentioned.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=190)** This is good if you're posting a message that you think people might miss, the notification will draw their attention to it.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/target-messages-with-mentions?u=76281980&t=196)** You may be in teams with several other members, using @ mentions lets you target messages to help draw the attention of specific people.

> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-delete-messages?u=76281980&t=118)** But if you need that option enabled, you need to request that from your company's Microsoft 365 administrator.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-delete-messages?u=76281980&t=125)** But it's nice to know when you post a message, it's not final and it can be changed.

> [!info]- Semantic Content

> **CLI Commands:** make (2)
> **UI Navigation:** click on (1)
> **Definitions:** is an  (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Add text-free reactions to messages
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In Teams, you can acknowledge messages without actually writing a response.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=4)** You can point your mouse cursor at a message, and when you're pointing at it, you'll see this row of buttons will appear at the top right.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=11)** That row will only be there when you're pointing at the message.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=14)** Now, the thumbs up, the heart, and the faces here are all reactions that you can apply to a message.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=19)** It's similar to liking a message on Facebook.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=22)** So all you need to do is select a reaction, and it will be applied to that message.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=26)** I can see it now below the message, and everybody else in this team will see that reaction.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=32)** So you can use this as a way to acknowledge that you saw and read a message but you don't actually have anything to say as a response.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=38)** Or you might use it to show that you're excited or enthusiastic about something.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=42)** And if you added a reaction by mistake, you can just click on it to remove it.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=48)** I'm going to go over to another channel in another team where I can see a message that somebody else reacted to.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=56)** So I see this surprised face under a message.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=59)** But you might be wondering, "How do I know who made this reaction?"
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=62)** Well, you can point your mouse cursor at it, and that will show me that it was Stewart who applied this reaction.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/add-text-free-reactions-to-messages?u=76281980&t=68)** So you might want to use reactions when you want to acknowledge a message but you don't have anything more to say.

#### Chat with people outside of your organization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/chat-with-people-outside-of-your-organization?u=76281980)

> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/get-set-up-for-calls-and-meetings?u=76281980&t=161)** This will open a menu where you can find more options during your meeting, but that's it for now.

> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/get-set-up-for-calls-and-meetings?u=76281980&t=166)** When you're finished with a meeting, you can click the Leave button up in the top right, that will leave the meeting and take you back to the normal Teams window.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/get-set-up-for-calls-and-meetings?u=76281980&t=174)** So please, take a moment and check your settings well before it's time to actually join your first meeting.

> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/start-a-meeting-on-demand?u=76281980&t=221)** So that's all you need to start a meeting on demand without scheduling it in advance.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** teams (8), [[Search]] (3)

#### Use breakout rooms in Microsoft Teams
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-breakout-rooms-in-microsoft-teams?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/use-breakout-rooms-in-microsoft-teams?u=76281980&t=0)** - During large group meetings, you may need to separate the attendees into smaller discussion groups.
>

#### Record and transcribe a meeting in Teams
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-your-screen-during-a-call-meeting-or-chat?u=76281980)

> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=247)** First, Copilot offers citations.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=250)** So these small numbers next to some of the lines here in the results, these are links to where it found this information.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=258)** Now in this case, all of these answers came from the same document, but if it found information from multiple sources, it would have different citations, and you could click on each one to go right to the original document or webpage or email or wherever it found that information.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=273)** Also, Copilot supports ongoing chats, so you can ask follow-up questions.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=279)** So in the chat field, I will ask, have I received email from any of them?
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=284)** And Copilot will remember the context of this conversation.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=288)** So I don't need to remind it which people or which document I was talking about.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=293)** And in this case, it found information from several of my email messages.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=297)** So we see different citations listed here.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=300)** And I can click on one of these citations.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=303)** It will take me to Outlook straight to the email message where it found this information.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=307)** For now, I'll close this and go back to Teams.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=311)** So you can have ongoing conversations, or at any time, you can click the New Chat button up at the top, which will reset, clearing Copilot's memory of that conversation and resetting to a new topic.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=323)** So Copilot can help you find information from your calendar, your emails, your team chats, your documents, and more.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=330)** And this is all protected by the security and privacy features in Microsoft 365.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=335)** This will never show you information from other people's communications or documents.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/streamline-your-work-with-copilot-ai-and-business-chat?u=76281980&t=340)** It will only use information that you have permission to see using any of the traditional tools in Microsoft 365 applications.

>

>

>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-meetings-more-secure-using-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=164)** If you are in a meeting with the watermark properly enabled, then your email address will be shown over the video feed in the meeting, or over any screen-sharing in the meeting, depending on which of these you enable.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-meetings-more-secure-using-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=178)** So, if somebody wanted secretly record their screen or take a picture of shared content, then leak that private sensitive information to another party, which would be a terrible breach of security, they would probably give up on that plan because their own email address will be stamped on that visual.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-meetings-more-secure-using-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=196)** That watermark immediately identifies the person responsible for leaking the sensitive information, so End-to-end encryption and watermarking are two ways to keep the content of your meetings much more secure and protected.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-meetings-more-secure-using-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=209)** Any user can enable these options when they create a meeting, but you must have the Teams Premium license and your Microsoft Administrator must enable these features in the Teams Admin settings.

> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/customize-meeting-experiences-with-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=265)** And if you do have Teams Premium, I encourage you to talk to your administrator and ask them to create templates with the pre-configured settings that you want.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/customize-meeting-experiences-with-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=275)** Remember, your administrator is usually somebody in your company's IT department who can help with your Teams configurations.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/customize-meeting-experiences-with-teams-premium?u=76281980&t=282)** So those are some of the most popular customization features available to users in an organization with Teams Premium.

#### Edit and collaborate on files
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=11)** Here in this channel, I could click on a file that has been shared to open it, or I could go over to the files tab and open a file from here.

> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=19)** So I'll click on this Microsoft Word document, and since I chose a Word document, I am able to edit that document right here in teams.

> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=46)** Now up at the top, you may see this button that says Open In Desktop.

> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=49)** If you have the Microsoft Word desktop application on your computer, that would launch the Word application and open that file.

> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=60)** You're just editing the same file that is stored in teams, so it does require a stable internet connection, and any changes that you make will be saved to the copy of the file that is stored in Teams.

> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=71)** And if you do that, you can take advantage of all of the features that are available here in the full desktop application.

> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=77)** But for now, I'm going to quit the Microsoft Word application and back here in Teams, I'll just click Continue so I can continue working on the document here.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=85)** And of course, any member of this Team can open this file the same way and can see all of the changes made by you and any other members of the Team.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=94)** In a moment, Stewart will open this document on his computer.

>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=105)** And if Stewart makes a change, I can see that change as it happens.

> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/edit-and-collaborate-on-files?u=76281980&t=110)** When multiple people are working on the shared document at the same time, it's called Co-Authoring.

#### Share Loop components in Teams and other applications
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Loop components let you share information with teammates without creating a separate document.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=5)** Loop components can be shared and reshared in other Microsoft applications and you can edit loop components even after they've been shared.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=14)** In teams you can go to a chat conversation or post a message in a team channel.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=18)** I'm in a chat conversation, so I'll go to the message field and there's a button here to create a loop component, and when I click that, it creates a loop component in the message field, but there are different types of components which can store different types of information.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=32)** By default, it makes a paragraph component, which can hold a title and a paragraph of text, but at the bottom you could switch this to be a different type of component.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=41)** So, I'll switch this to be a task list and it changes the formatting of the component.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=46)** Now I'm going to scroll to the top of this component and there is still a title field here, we can't see it until we click on it, but then I can add a title here, then I'll start adding some information to this list.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=62)** I've added two items to the list, and I can click where it says "Add task" and then keep adding more.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=70)** When you have everything you want in the component, you can simply send the message as normal.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=75)** (digital pulsing) Now that I've shared it, anybody I've sent the component to will be able to see it here.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=81)** Now, when Stewart opens a component on his computer, I will see his account icon up at the top, and even better, my teammates can edit the component even after it's been shared.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=99)** So, I can see that Stewart has added a new task and he's starting to make some assignments in these tasks, and I can see those changes (digital pulsing) as he's making them.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=111)** Now, in the top right of the component, I can click the access button to see who has seen the component.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=117)** Now, this does not list everybody it has been shared with, only the people who have actually seen it, but one of the best things about a loop component is that they can be reshared in other applications.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=129)** Also near the top right you can click the copy button, that copy's a link to the component, so I can paste it in another application.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=137)** I'll go over to Outlook where I've started writing an email message.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=142)** I can just paste that component right here in this message, and, of course, you can create components in Outlook, as well.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=152)** When you're writing an email message, you can go to the Insert ribbon up at the top, and there's an option here to insert loop components that way.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=161)** You can also add loop components to documents in Microsoft Word online, and to whiteboards in Microsoft Whiteboard and support for loop components may be added in other Microsoft applications in the future, but here in Outlook, I could send this email and any recipients who are in my organization will be able to see it and edit the loop component in Outlook, and I could continue to work with it over here in Microsoft Teams.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/share-loop-components-in-teams-and-other-applications?u=76281980&t=185)** Loop components are a great way to share information in several Microsoft applications without creating new documents.

#### Customize channel tabs in Teams
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/customize-channel-tabs-in-teams?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/customize-channel-tabs-in-teams?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You can add extra tabs to your conversation channels, which can give your teammates easy access to important supplemental materials.
>

> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=77)** Also, Teams can keep running in the background even if you close the window.

> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=82)** You can disable that here as well.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=84)** Of course, these options are not available in the web version of Teams.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=88)** Next we'll go over to the Privacy category.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=91)** I'll select that over on the left, and if you set your status in Teams to Do Not Disturb, that will block notifications for all incoming messages.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=101)** But if there are any people who you consider to be a high priority and you do want to see alerts from messages from those people, even when you're set to Do Not Disturb, you can add them to this priority access list.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=114)** Just click this priority access button, search for people in your organization, and add them to the list.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=120)** Next, over on the left, I want to select the section for notifications and activity.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=126)** Now there are lots of things that may trigger notifications in Teams.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=130)** These are alerts that pop up on your screen when you get a new chat message or somebody mentions you in a Team channel or you have a meeting reminder.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=139)** Lots of different things, and you can go through these options and change how and when notifications will appear for channel conversations and private chats, for meeting reminders, and more.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=152)** But there is an important option up at the top, and the option you see here may be different depending on whether you're using Teams on Windows, on a Mac, or in a web browser.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=162)** But there should be some option like this, which can disable all notifications except for calls and meetings, or some users may see some controls to integrate Teams notifications into the main system notifications on your computer.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=177)** Just be aware, if you use multiple computers or mobile devices, you will have to set your notification preferences on each device.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=185)** These options you choose here only apply to this one computer.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=190)** And let's look at one more category in Settings.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=193)** On the left, we'll choose appearance and accessibility, and here you have the option to set different themes.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=199)** You can choose the light theme or you could choose the dark theme, or you could just tell it to choose whichever mode you have set in Windows or Mac.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=209)** There's also a high contrast option, which can help some people with visual impairments.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=215)** But for now, I'll just reset this to follow the theme set by my operating system.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=220)** And if you continue to scroll through the appearance and accessibility category, there are also several options here that may help you if you or your teammates have visual or hearing impairments.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=231)** So I think these are the most essential settings you should look at, but more importantly, you know where to go when you need to find and change settings in Teams.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-notification-options?u=76281980&t=241)** You may want to explore these a bit or just come and search through here when you need to make some adjustments.

> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-permissions-in-a-team?u=76281980&t=216)** This shows a summary of all of the teams that you are a member of, along with many of those management options.

> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-permissions-in-a-team?u=76281980&t=222)** You can quickly see whether you are an owner or a normal member on each team, you can see how many people are in each team, and you can see whether a team is public or private.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-permissions-in-a-team?u=76281980&t=234)** This lock icon means that this team is private.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-permissions-in-a-team?u=76281980&t=238)** And you can click the button with three dots all the way on the right side next to a team to get that same menu that we saw before for all of those management options.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/adjust-settings-and-permissions-in-a-team?u=76281980&t=247)** So if you are a team owner, you've got lots of tools to manage how those teams work, including permissions for normal members.

>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-the-teams-interface-easier-to-see-25634946?u=76281980&t=204)** If there are people on your team who have visual impairments, this can really help them to see and understand you.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-the-teams-interface-easier-to-see-25634946?u=76281980&t=210)** Or if you're in a meeting with somebody whose primary language is not the same as the language that you are speaking, they may rely on a variety of facial cues or facial expressions, or even mild lip reading to fully understand you.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-the-teams-interface-easier-to-see-25634946?u=76281980&t=224)** So I recommend you use a good clean video frame with plenty of contrast.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-the-teams-interface-easier-to-see-25634946?u=76281980&t=229)** That might mean that you keep a very clean space behind you and you use good lighting during your meetings, but if you can't do that, a blurred background or a virtual background like this one can really help.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/make-the-teams-interface-easier-to-see-25634946?u=76281980&t=240)** So those are a few options you have to make the Teams interface easier to see for yourself and even for your teammates.

> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=129)** But as we'll see in a moment, I will not be able to set this person as an interpreter.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=134)** I will be able to set Madisyn though, because she is a guest member of one of my teams.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=140)** Okay, next I'll click the button at the top for Meeting options, then go to the section for Roles and we see the option for language interpretation.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=150)** So I'll turn that on, and then in this field I can choose the person who will act as the interpreter.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=156)** Notice that Madisyn is available but that other guest user who I invited using their email address is not.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=163)** I'm going to choose Madisyn, then I need to define the languages.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=167)** Madisyn will be translating from Italian to English
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=176)** so I'll set those there.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=178)** And below that you have the option to add even more interpreters.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=181)** So you can have multiple language interpretations available for different attendees that understand different languages.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=187)** But for now, I'll just stick with one interpreter.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=190)** I'll click Save, then I'll click the Send button to send this meeting invitation.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=196)** Now I can see that meeting here on my calendar, and let's see what happens when I join that meeting.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=200)** So I'll click on that meeting, I'll click the Join button, and here on the join screen, I'll click Join now.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=207)** And I see this message immediately letting me know that language interpretation is available.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=213)** You could just click this button and enable that right here.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=216)** Or if you close this panel, you can always get back to those settings by clicking the More button in the toolbar at the top, then go to Language and speech, then choose Interpretation language.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=228)** And from this menu, I want to hear English, so I'll choose English and then I can use this slider to set the balance.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=236)** When somebody is speaking Italian in this meeting, I can decide whether I want to hear more of the original Italian person speaking or more of the interpreter's voice.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=246)** So I can drag this slider, then click Confirm.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=249)** And now obviously we don't have those people all in this meeting, but if we did, whenever the Italian people are speaking, I would hear the audio from the interpreter as they translate.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-teams-essential-training-23929395/designate-an-interpreter-during-a-meeting?u=76281980&t=260)** So assigning a language interpreter may be a very valuable step if you have meetings with people who speak different languages.
